<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer6600137730351560126">FOUR VERY DIFFERENT FRIENDS. ONE PAIR OF MAGICAL PANTS. AND A SUMMER APART ...<br /><br />We, the Sisterhood, hereby instate the following rules to govern the use of the Traveling Pants:<br /><br />1. You must never wash the Pants.<br /><br />2. You must never double-cuff the Pants. It's tacky. There will never be a time when this will not be tacky.<br /><br />3. You must never say the word "phat" while wearing the Pant</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6600137730351560126">FOUR VERY DIFFERENT FRIENDS. ONE PAIR OF MAGICAL PANTS. AND A SUMMER APART ...<br /><br />We, the Sisterhood, hereby instate the following rules to govern the use of the Traveling Pants:<br /><br />1. You must never wash the Pants.<br /><br />2. You must never double-cuff the Pants. It's tacky. There will never be a time when this will not be tacky.<br /><br />3. You must never say the word "phat" while wearing the Pants. You must also never think "I am fat" while wearing the Pants.<br /><br />4. You must never let a boy take off the Pants (although you may take them off yourself in his presence).<br /><br />5. You must not pick your nose while wearing the Pants. You may, however, scratch casually your nostril while really kind of picking.<br /><br />6. Upon our reunion, you must follow the proper procedures for documenting your time in the Pants.<br /><br />7. You must write to your Sisters throughout the summer, no matter how much fun you are having without them.<br /><br />8. You must pass the Pants along to your Sister according to the specifications set down by the Sisterhood. Failures to comply will result in a sever spanking upon our reunion.<br /><br />9. You must not wear the Pants with a tucked-in shirt and belt. See rule #2.<br /><br />10. Remember: Pants = love. Love your pals. Love yourself.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6600137730351560126">...more</a>

      </div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1739081">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2610112899197117795"> A sparkling breath of fresh air, this book captures the spirit of friendship in the most charming and sauciest manner possible. <br /><br /> The book is a far cry from the regular breed of YA novels which seem to dwell on the fixed notions that young girls basically fall into two main groups: One, the hatefully pretty, perpetually scheming Prom Queens with their nastier than “week-ol’ milk” cliques! And at the other end of the rainbow, the brave under-dog...not much to look at, the general do-gooder, the f</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2610112899197117795"> A sparkling breath of fresh air, this book captures the spirit of friendship in the most charming and sauciest manner possible. <br /><br /> The book is a far cry from the regular breed of YA novels which seem to dwell on the fixed notions that young girls basically fall into two main groups: One, the hatefully pretty, perpetually scheming Prom Queens with their nastier than “week-ol’ milk” cliques! And at the other end of the rainbow, the brave under-dog...not much to look at, the general do-gooder, the faithful confidante and to nicely round it off, more often than not, armed with an IQ formidable enough to gain entry into MENSA.<br /><br /> Breaking the age-old mould with insouciance, <strong>Ann Brashares</strong> creates a world where it is possible for four friends, as different as chalk and cheese to form a deeply satisfying friendship. They care for each other, love each other, put aside fights and misunderstandings with a careless shrug and offer unstinted, non-judgmental support any time, everytime.<br /><br /><strong>Lena</strong>, the reluctant beauty; feisty, big-tushied <strong>Carmen</strong>; the anti-everything, mad-at-the-world <strong>Tibby</strong> and the over-achieving, statuesque athlete <strong>Bridget</strong> are friends; literally since birth (<em>their mums shared a preggers-aerobics class</em>). Having grown up in each other’s pockets, along comes a summer when the four are parted for the first time. Lena is off to Greece to meet her grandparents; Carmen to spend some quality time with her divorced dad in South Carolina; Bridget to Baja, California for summer camp and Tibby, the impotent rebel is stuck at home, cutting a minimum wage at Wallman’s. <br /><br /> A well-worn pair of soft jeans bought at a thrift-shop by Carmen but never-tried becomes an unexpected bond to hold the four pals together. Despite their vastly different body proportions, the seemingly-magical pair of jeans fits each of them like a dream……hugging the right curves, resting gracefully on the varying waistlines, making each teen feel sexy and infusing them with much-needed confidence. <br /><br /> They make a pact (<em>complete with a set of serious-cum-nonsensical rules</em>) to circulate the pants amongst themselves throughout their vacation, passing it on when the time is right. Thus begins the saga of the Sisterhood……<br /><br /> As the long, glorious summer unravels, the pants become a source and symbol of the generous support which the sisterhood provides to each of the four buddies as they face unwieldy situations. Sucker-punched by new emotions, the friends absorb confidence from their ever-reliable ‘magical pants’. For each, the pants seem to be infused with the strength and support of their fellow friends. <br /><br /> Brimming with energy and vitality, the book effortlessly hops between the four friends as they deal with life, love and all-things ‘teen-achy’. One of the best coming-of-age books in a long time, it’s a must read for everyone who is-a-teen, was-a-teen and will soon be-a-quakin’ in your boots-teen.<br /><br /> It’s a tough world out there, but when you got your SIST –AHS, life’s just a wee bit more bearable.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2610112899197117795">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_5995522">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/5995522" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/94054-briynne" class="left imgcol" title="Briynne"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1225157665p2/94054.jpg" alt="Briynne" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/5995522?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 10, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/94054-briynne" class="user" title="Briynne">Briynne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/452306.The_Sisterhood_of_the_Traveling_Pants" title="Hardcover 9780385729338" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer5995522">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer458619117151314438">This is beginning to feel a little too familiar, but here's yet another disapointment from my YA Lit class. First, I should state that I have never liked the whole "girl power" thing. I guess I always felt intelligent/empowered enough as a teenager to not have to rely on books like this to show me how fantastic it is to be female. Also, generally speaking, I find large groups of girls terrifying, especially at the high school age. So lots of pre-existing strikes against this book. <br /><br />As for the sto</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText458619117151314438">This is beginning to feel a little too familiar, but here's yet another disapointment from my YA Lit class. First, I should state that I have never liked the whole "girl power" thing. I guess I always felt intelligent/empowered enough as a teenager to not have to rely on books like this to show me how fantastic it is to be female. Also, generally speaking, I find large groups of girls terrifying, especially at the high school age. So lots of pre-existing strikes against this book. <br /><br />As for the story itself: blah. <br /><br />Complaint the first: I dislike the fomulatic "four girls with four neat, distinctive personalities" thing. I mean come on - all my friends in high school were pretty much the exact same as me, but with different colors of hair and varying degrees of niceness. <br /><br />Complaint the second: I was unconvinced by every single one of the characters. Lena I liked the best, but I still didn't buy the whole "I don't want people to like me 'cause I'm pretty" thing. Realistically, most pretty teenagers seem fairly psyched by their good fortune and run with it. Maybe if she was in her twenties (still a maybe), but at fifteen? <br /><br />Similarly, the one who played soccer and her agressive hitting on the coach senario. Maybe it was realistic, but if it is, I didn't grow up with girls like that. It all seemed a little contrived to me. Even at fifteen we all had a pretty good handle on the word "skank", and the lack of it being thrown around by anyone made this seem less real-world. Girls aren't nice - if one person has the nerve to flirt with the camp idol (especially if she is sucessful), she isn't cheered on and adored for it. She is hated, whispered about, and called lots of fun names for it. Or, at least where I came from. <br /><br />Complaint the third: the kid with cancer. Not to be cold (or, perhaps "colder" would be more accurate), but dying does not make you self-aware, wise, and interesting all by itself so far as I know. Yet somehow books/movies just can't resist the wise-beyond-her-years dying kid. It would make a lot more sense and be a lot more authentic if she were just mad, not a slightly rebellious Yoda. <br /><br />Complaint the fourth: The stupid pants. I hated the completely idiotic premise of the book. Seriously. Magic pants that fit everyone? That's the best that could be thought up? Not good. Not good at all. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="458619117151314438">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11670620269519281665">I read the Sisterhood of the Traveling Pants when I was 11 years old. It was the most comforting thing to me at the time when I was in middle school a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11670620269519281665">I read the Sisterhood of the Traveling Pants when I was 11 years old. It was the most comforting thing to me at the time when I was in middle school and had no friends. The idea of girls different from me and us caring about each other was great. Kind of hokey, but different and exactly what I needed when I started to read this series. The book is four stories intertwined into a story of friendship, love and sisterhood. Where no one is judged by if they are plus size or sleep with their coach. Bridget's mom had died. She was trying to get over her with Eric and Eric liked Bridget. They both had a connection if even a little hard for her to handle at age 15 does not make her a "slut." That is shaming a lot of woman. Yet it is still not okay that Lena is shy about her beauty? Maybe it's because she doesn't find it to be the most important thing. Is that unrealistic to you? Baliegh had Cancer. She was a special character in this book because she changed Tibby dramatically. The author was not using Cancer but making a statement about how horrible it is and why not? I am sorry your friends were "all the same" growing up but you really don't know enough about feminism if you don't understand that every girl is different and this is a celebration of that as well as the trials of coming of age. You just don't get it.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_2696241">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2696241" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/41783-erin" class="left imgcol" title="Erin"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1194215785p2/41783.jpg" alt="Erin" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/2696241?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 03, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/41783-erin" class="user" title="Erin">Erin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/41783-erin?shelf=yafiction" class="actionLinkLite">yafiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer2696241">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15856549079154374083"><em>We, the Sisterhood, hereby instate the following rules to govern the use of the Traveling Pants.<br />1.) You must never wash the Pants.<br />2.) You must never double-cuff the Pants. It's tacky. There will never be a time when this will not be tacky.<br />3.) You must never say the word "phat" while wearing the Pants. You must also never think "I am fat" while wearing the Pants...</em><br /><br />So begins the first summer apart for four friends: Lena, who is going to visit her grandparents in Greece with her sister; Carmen, hea</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15856549079154374083"><em>We, the Sisterhood, hereby instate the following rules to govern the use of the Traveling Pants.<br />1.) You must never wash the Pants.<br />2.) You must never double-cuff the Pants. It's tacky. There will never be a time when this will not be tacky.<br />3.) You must never say the word "phat" while wearing the Pants. You must also never think "I am fat" while wearing the Pants...</em><br /><br />So begins the first summer apart for four friends: Lena, who is going to visit her grandparents in Greece with her sister; Carmen, heading south to see her father; Bridget, going to a soccer camp in Mexico; and Tibbie, the only one of the four to be stuck at home with a summer job. In order to feel a bit closer despite the distance, the friends find a pair of pants they profess to be "magical" -- it fits all four of them perfectly -- and form a "Sisterhood" around the pants. They are mailed back and forth from girl to girl as needed; they are all wearing the pants during a significant moment of theirs from that summer.<br /><br />Lena bonds with her grandparents and learns that not every guy who is attracted to her is shallow. Carmen finds out that her father is living with his fiancee and her two children, and must cope with the shock and find a way to fit in. Bridget crushes on a coach from the soccer camp, and finds the forbidden relationship yet another challenge. Tibbie meets a younger girl who, despite her young age, teaches Tibbie that there is more to a person than outward appearance.<br /><br />Ann Brashares has written four Sisterhood books, this being the first in the series. It is definitely a must-read for teen girls.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15856549079154374083">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer6930682256244717028">Wow! If you are a teen girl looking for some love stories between friends and their SUPER-HOT boyfriends, well look no further then the Sisterhood of the Traveling Pants series! This book is about the 4 best friends Bridget, Carmen, Tibby, and Lena when they split up for the summer. With the Pants binding them together wherever they go, their summers are no longer lonely. The Pants witness all break - ups and get togethers and are often shipped with hysterical letters that will make you laugh ou</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6930682256244717028">Wow! If you are a teen girl looking for some love stories between friends and their SUPER-HOT boyfriends, well look no further then the Sisterhood of the Traveling Pants series! This book is about the 4 best friends Bridget, Carmen, Tibby, and Lena when they split up for the summer. With the Pants binding them together wherever they go, their summers are no longer lonely. The Pants witness all break - ups and get togethers and are often shipped with hysterical letters that will make you laugh out loud! I think my favorite is the love - hate relationship between Eric and Bridget, but I can't tell you, so read to find out!</span>

      <a href="/user/show/754037-julie" class="user" title="Julie">Julie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/452306.The_Sisterhood_of_the_Traveling_Pants" title="Hardcover 9780385729338" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer11907824'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer11907824">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8946254394413429223">I saw the movie first and kind of liked it. So, of course I thought "Well the book is always better than the movie" so I decided to read it, even though its written for teens and I wasn't too sure I could relate. I guess I couldn't because this is one time I liked the movie a lot better than the book. I mean really, how many 15/16 year old girls do you know who's parents let them go trapezing all over the world (in Lena's case literally) and don't think twice about it. Come to think of it how ma</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8946254394413429223">I saw the movie first and kind of liked it. So, of course I thought "Well the book is always better than the movie" so I decided to read it, even though its written for teens and I wasn't too sure I could relate. I guess I couldn't because this is one time I liked the movie a lot better than the book. I mean really, how many 15/16 year old girls do you know who's parents let them go trapezing all over the world (in Lena's case literally) and don't think twice about it. Come to think of it how many 15/16 year old girls have the money to it even if they're parents really are that totally oblivious. Not to mention Bailey, who is roaming around with Tibby all summer despite a major medical condition that would most certainly keep her slowed down, if not out completely.<br /><br />The main characters in this book are flat and, frankly, boring and the situations they are in are really not very believable. The adults are almost completely absent, and when they are present they are made out to be selfish, stupid, unaware, or all of the above.<br /><br />This is a perfect teen angst novel that I'm sure will appeal to teenagers everywhere who will find this a wonderful book about girls their own age who get to do what they want when they want and have really no real consequences. Not to mention the whole "My friends are my life" theme which will also appeal to a younger angrier audience. For those of us who have battled through those misunderstood years and know that life doesn't work quite that way, well...this novel will leave most ADULTS cold.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12367940073130144869">Maybe because Bailey was dying they decided to let her LIVE a little? Dying doesn't always mean you are confined to a bed for the rest of your life. H</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12367940073130144869">Maybe because Bailey was dying they decided to let her LIVE a little? Dying doesn't always mean you are confined to a bed for the rest of your life. Having a terminal illness doesn't always mean staying in bed and not riding your bike. It's all about what you CAN do until the end and Bailey was living her life the best she could. <br /><br />As for the other girls: Bee had a soccer camp in Mexico and I know there are a lot of teen girls (at least ten years ago, at the time this book was written), that go to soccer camps around the world. Her dad also was not that present and her mom had just died, so the family was grieving and maybe she needed to go away for a while. Maybe they understood that. Lena was visiting her grandparents for the first time, so that's easy to explain. <br /><br />As you can tell, I liked the book and I like the whole series, including Sisterhood Everlasting, which is the companion book. Some parts might be a little unrealistic (like four very different sized girls fitting into a pair of pants), but a lot of the stuff they deal with is realistic. It was to me when I was 18, anyway.</span>

  <a href="/user/show/6478831-charlotte" class="left imgcol" title="Charlotte"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Charlotte" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/348995047?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 26, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6478831-charlotte" class="user" title="Charlotte">Charlotte</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/452306.The_Sisterhood_of_the_Traveling_Pants" title="Hardcover 9780385729338" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6478831-charlotte?shelf=hated-main-character" class="actionLinkLite">hated-main-character</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6478831-charlotte?shelf=dont-bother" class="actionLinkLite">dont-bother</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6478831-charlotte?shelf=this-book-bores-your-math-teacher" class="actionLinkLite">this-book-bores-your-math-teacher</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6478831-charlotte?shelf=blah-blah-blah" class="actionLinkLite">blah-blah-blah</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer348995047">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8492980415542141739">What an <em>annoying</em> book. <br />I was going to write snarky, individual letters to each of the characters in succession, but then I realized that it was a pointless endeveaour since all the letters would end up the same, anyway. Why, you ask? Because all the characters are the same.<br />Would you like to know some personality traits? It's like the author picked one or two for each of the characters and then relied on either one or the other to simply parasail each of the girls through the book. <br /><br />There was Lena</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8492980415542141739">What an <em>annoying</em> book. <br />I was going to write snarky, individual letters to each of the characters in succession, but then I realized that it was a pointless endeveaour since all the letters would end up the same, anyway. Why, you ask? Because all the characters are the same.<br />Would you like to know some personality traits? It's like the author picked one or two for each of the characters and then relied on either one or the other to simply parasail each of the girls through the book. <br /><br />There was Lena, who was beautiful and shy. But we all know that shy girls have a bevy of passion hidden up inside, right?<br />There was Bridget, who was a flirtatious athelete. Her plotline involves flirting with a guy, I don't know, ten years older than her? More? <br />There was Carmen, who was either angry or passive through the book and is the least interesting character in the whole series. I'm glad, however, for this. In the second book she morphs into a semi-interesting absolute <em>brat</em>. <br />And then there was Tibby. Thank goodness for Tibby. She was absolutely the only character with a personality or an interesting story in the whole book. Tibby, get better friends. Or none at all. Considering Tibby, she'd probably go with <em>none at all</em>.<br />In fact, the only storyline I enjoyed was Tibby and Bailey's, and I found myself flipping through Carmen's, Lena's and Bridget's chapters to get to hers. <br />Although I did stop at Bridget's a couple of times to see if she actually did hook up with Mr. Coach Man. Which is illegal, since she's 16 and he's... uh. 26?<br />And here we get to what bothered me. Why didn't someone arrest Eric? And why are Bridget's friends so irresponsible? When Bridget basically tells them that she slept with a guy over 18, the only reaction she gets are some wide eyes. Don't you want to, you know, <em>report the rapist to the police?</em><br />Oh, I know it was Bridget's choice, and all that. And I would semi-understand if he was an interesting character or she was an interesting character and they had semi-interesting chemistry together. But they didn't. They had mutual attraction based on mutual sexiness, and didn't really bother to get to know each other much more, even in the next three books. Not that there's anything to know.<br /><br /><br />Dull. Dull, dull, dull. If it had been a novella featuring only Tibby, I might have found it a lot better, maybe even given it four stars. But with the rest of the <s>baggage</s> characters tagging along for the ride... no, thanks. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8492980415542141739">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_368657051">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/368657051" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/10961933-shannon-leaninglights" class="left imgcol" title="Shannon (leaninglights)"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1441470068p2/10961933.jpg" alt="Shannon (leaninglights)" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/368657051?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 02, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/10961933-shannon-leaninglights" class="user" title="Shannon (leaninglights)">Shannon (leaninglights)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/452306.The_Sisterhood_of_the_Traveling_Pants" title="Hardcover 9780385729338" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer368657051">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1999910227357612137">I really love this series. I think these were the first multiple perspective books I ever read and I really adored being back in the world of Lena, Tibby, Bee &amp; Carmen. I feel like everyone can cast themselves as one of the girls, or at least a mixture of them. <br />This is the story of the first summer the girls spend apart, each going on different adventures and stepping out into the world of grown-ups and real life. The first book takes place over the summer of their 15th (almost 16) year. We</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1999910227357612137">I really love this series. I think these were the first multiple perspective books I ever read and I really adored being back in the world of Lena, Tibby, Bee &amp; Carmen. I feel like everyone can cast themselves as one of the girls, or at least a mixture of them. <br />This is the story of the first summer the girls spend apart, each going on different adventures and stepping out into the world of grown-ups and real life. The first book takes place over the summer of their 15th (almost 16) year. We see each of the girls go through a multitude of growth and life experience and Ann's honestly is really refreshing.<br />I kind of wish more contemporary books where like this - less angsty and more awkward, full of mistakes and OOPS moments :)<br />I also listened to the audiobook for parts of the story and I really recommend it! I thought it was really well done.<br />When I was younger, I would have said I was a Bee/Carmen kind of girl, but now that I'm older and know myself a little better, I'm actually a Lena/Carmen kind of girl! What about you?<br />I definitely give this book 5 stars, though I admit my rating will never be unbiased, as I read these books as a teenager and have such an affinity for them in my heart!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1999910227357612137">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_42174300">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/42174300" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1717549-antof9" class="left imgcol" title="Antof9"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1228251264p2/1717549.jpg" alt="Antof9" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/42174300?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 06, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1717549-antof9" class="user" title="Antof9">Antof9</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/452306.The_Sisterhood_of_the_Traveling_Pants" title="Hardcover 9780385729338" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1717549-antof9?shelf=made-me-cry" class="actionLinkLite">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1717549-antof9?shelf=faves" class="actionLinkLite">faves</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1717549-antof9?shelf=2004-read" class="actionLinkLite">2004-read</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1717549-antof9?shelf=charming" class="actionLinkLite">charming</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1717549-antof9?shelf=couldn-t-put-it-down" class="actionLinkLite">couldn-t-put-it-down</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer42174300">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6116649966931942645">Must quote from the back of the book, as I love it :)<br /><br />We, the Sisterhood, hereby instate the following rules to govern the use of the Traveling Pants:<br />2. You must never double-cuff the Pants. It's tacky. There will never be a time when this will not be tacky.<br />4. You must never let a boy take off the Pants (although you may take them off yourself in his presence).<br />5. You must not pick your nose while wearing the Pants. You may, however, scratch casually at your nostril while really kind of picking.<br /><br />I</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6116649966931942645">Must quote from the back of the book, as I love it :)<br /><br />We, the Sisterhood, hereby instate the following rules to govern the use of the Traveling Pants:<br />2. You must never double-cuff the Pants. It's tacky. There will never be a time when this will not be tacky.<br />4. You must never let a boy take off the Pants (although you may take them off yourself in his presence).<br />5. You must not pick your nose while wearing the Pants. You may, however, scratch casually at your nostril while really kind of picking.<br /><br />I have to say it. I loved this book! I've been putting off my book review because frankly, it's like writing a book report on a great movie or dream. <br /><br />I love the idea of The Septembers, a bunch of girls all born at the same time. Maybe it's special to me because *I'm* a September.<br /><br />These girls are friends their entire lives (well to age 15, at least), and that too is something that touches me. My dad was in the Air Force and we moved a lot. I don't have any friends who have known me since birth, and I've always been jealous of people who do.<br /><br />For a book written for teens, there are some beautifully written passages, and some very insightful sections. This author doesn't "talk down" to the reader at all. I love the description of Lena's sunset in Greece: "The sunset was too beautiful. It almost made Lena feel panicked because she couldn't save it. . . . She perched on her windowsill, gazing at the lurid sun soaking into the Caldera, trying to appreciate it even though she couldn't have it. Why did she always feel she had to <em>do</em> something in the face of beauty?" I had two thoughts when I read this -- 1. that I often feel the same way in the face of beauty, and 2. this makes me think of people who take pictures (for the future), but don't enjoy the moment they are actually taking the pictures of.<br /><br />Another passage that said exactly something I have felt many times: "Her eyes were full. They dripped. From sadness, or strangeness, or love. They were the kind of tears that came when she was just too full. She needed to make a little room." Do you know this feeling? Wow, I do. What a wonderful way to write it.<br /><br />SPOILER ALERT:<br /><br />When Tibby's pet dies and Tibby is in denial, it requires some processing to realize Mimi is gone. "Tibby held her up high, in one hand. Mimi hated that. She usually scrambled her sharp little nails against Tibby's wrist. Dawning on her both slowly and panic-fast was the knowledge that this wasn't Mimi anymore. This was left-over Mimi." OH, how I know what this means! I wanted to see my dad's body after he died, but when I saw him, it was somehow unfulfilling. It was left-over dad, I think.<br /><br />When her friend Bailey dies too, Brashares writes the most beautiful tribute for the living: "She was alive, and they were dead. She had to try to make her life big. As big as she could. She promised Bailey she would keep playing." This is a fabulous challenge for those of us who have lost someone. What a charge! We must go on living. And live big :)<br /><br />This is a great book! I laughed, I cried.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6116649966931942645">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15693563210480062176">I was almost ashamed to love this book, because I'm REALLY not one for "chick lit"...give me Gothic or intrigue any day! However, I think this series is really exceptional. The experiences cannot be typified -although there is romance, I appreciate how it does not fall into the "crush/agony/happily-ever-after" triptych that is common to most "chick lit" novels. <br /><br />I think Ann Brashares is remarkably gifted at describing emotions and experiences -she chooses seemingly minor incidents and trains her</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15693563210480062176">I was almost ashamed to love this book, because I'm REALLY not one for "chick lit"...give me Gothic or intrigue any day! However, I think this series is really exceptional. The experiences cannot be typified -although there is romance, I appreciate how it does not fall into the "crush/agony/happily-ever-after" triptych that is common to most "chick lit" novels. <br /><br />I think Ann Brashares is remarkably gifted at describing emotions and experiences -she chooses seemingly minor incidents and trains her descriptive powers on them until you see the intricacies just as she does. I would be interested to see her in another genre -maybe historical fiction? I think she would excel at that -she could really enliven history.</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1315230111?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 22, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/44166225-kristen-kaymaldo" class="user" title="Kristen (kaymaldo)">Kristen (kaymaldo)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/452306.The_Sisterhood_of_the_Traveling_Pants" title="Hardcover 9780385729338" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/44166225-kristen-kaymaldo?shelf=adapted-books" class="actionLinkLite">adapted-books</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/44166225-kristen-kaymaldo?shelf=100-book-challenge-2015" class="actionLinkLite">100-book-challenge-2015</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/44166225-kristen-kaymaldo?shelf=reviews" class="actionLinkLite">reviews</a>,

              <a href="/review/list/44166225-kristen-kaymaldo?shelf=contemporary" class="actionLinkLite">contemporary</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/44166225-kristen-kaymaldo?shelf=coming-of-age" class="actionLinkLite">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/44166225-kristen-kaymaldo?shelf=love-story" class="actionLinkLite">love-story</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/44166225-kristen-kaymaldo?shelf=tearjerker" class="actionLinkLite">tearjerker</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/44166225-kristen-kaymaldo?shelf=travel" class="actionLinkLite">travel</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/44166225-kristen-kaymaldo?shelf=friendship" class="actionLinkLite">friendship</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/44166225-kristen-kaymaldo?shelf=diversity" class="actionLinkLite">diversity</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/44166225-kristen-kaymaldo?shelf=summer" class="actionLinkLite">summer</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/44166225-kristen-kaymaldo?shelf=realistic-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/44166225-kristen-kaymaldo?shelf=multiple-pov" class="actionLinkLite">multiple-pov</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1315230111">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3752405559415132840">I was stuck in a mini book slump so I decided to throw it back to a summer classic with <a title="The Sisterhood of the Traveling Pants (Sisterhood, #1) by Ann Brashares" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/452306.The_Sisterhood_of_the_Traveling_Pants__Sisterhood___1_"> The Sisterhood of the Traveling Pants</a>. I remembered a good amount of what happened from when I read the book and watched the movie when I was younger, but after reading it now, it really made me want to go back and finish the series. <br /><br />Even though this book is about a magical pair of jeans shared among friends, I really enjoyed how realistic it was. Carmen, Lena, and Tibby have my favorite story lines. Carmen'</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3752405559415132840">I was stuck in a mini book slump so I decided to throw it back to a summer classic with <a title="The Sisterhood of the Traveling Pants (Sisterhood, #1) by Ann Brashares" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/452306.The_Sisterhood_of_the_Traveling_Pants__Sisterhood___1_"> The Sisterhood of the Traveling Pants</a>. I remembered a good amount of what happened from when I read the book and watched the movie when I was younger, but after reading it now, it really made me want to go back and finish the series. <br /><br />Even though this book is about a magical pair of jeans shared among friends, I really enjoyed how realistic it was. Carmen, Lena, and Tibby have my favorite story lines. Carmen's phone call with her dad has always been a scene that stood out to be in the book and the movie, and even after reading it again, the whole situation still had me in tears. I appreciated Lena's story and how she found a connection to her grandfather. I also liked that <a title="Ann Brashares" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3681.Ann_Brashares"> Ann Brashares</a> didn't push the romance for Lena and Kostos. They liked each other, but <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[it wasn't an annoying instalust story. It took the whole book before they actually admitted their feelings for each other and kissed <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I would've liked for them to have more time to actually get to know each other, but even the small scenes where Lena is just observing him and noticing things about him are sweet and I'm hoping we see their love story grow in the second book. Tibby's story was heartbreaking. I think Bailey is a great character and I loved seeing Tibby and Bailey's friendship grow over the summer. Bailey really opened Tibby up to seeing the world in a new way. Things get a little conflicted when it comes to Bridget's summer. I think Brashares has given Bridget some interesting character traits. She is manic and headstrong and has high highs and low lows. It makes me wonder if she deals with <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[mental illness in the rest of the series, or if this is just a story of a high school girl who lost her way and is trying to find herself again <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I didn't like Eric and Bridget's storyline together and think he acted inappropriately in a position of authority. I'm also not a huge sports person, so for me the soccer camp plot was the least appealing.<br /><br />The Sisterhood of the Traveling Pants was a quick summer read that shows just how important friendship is. Tibby, Bridget, Carmen, and Lena support each other through everything they go through that summer and prove that even distance can't shatter their bond. It had me feeling all the feels, wishing for magic pants, and praying I win the lottery so I can go to Greece. Now I want to read the rest of the series and re-watch the films.<br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.youtube.com/kaymaldo">YouTube</a> | <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.twitter.com/kaymaldo">Twitter</a> | <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.facebook.com/kaymaldo">Facebook</a> | <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.instagram.com/kaymaldo1">Instagram</a> | <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.kristenmaldonado.com">Website</a><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3752405559415132840">...more</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1489224-lisa" class="user" title="Lisa">Lisa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/452306.The_Sisterhood_of_the_Traveling_Pants" title="Hardcover 9780385729338" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1489224-lisa?shelf=contemporary" class="actionLinkLite">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer587884162">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1683791837889087948">This book took me completely by surprise. I wasn't planning on reading it but the movie was coming on and I decided I should read the book first before watching the film. <em>The Sisterhood of the Traveling Pants</em> is a story with an awful premise that was surprisingly well-executed. <br /><br />Going into it, I expected some silly, shallow book about four teenage girls falling in love over one summer, but instead this book focused on the exploration of family dysfunction, death, and the bonds of friendship. <em>The</em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1683791837889087948">This book took me completely by surprise. I wasn't planning on reading it but the movie was coming on and I decided I should read the book first before watching the film. <em>The Sisterhood of the Traveling Pants</em> is a story with an awful premise that was surprisingly well-executed. <br /><br />Going into it, I expected some silly, shallow book about four teenage girls falling in love over one summer, but instead this book focused on the exploration of family dysfunction, death, and the bonds of friendship. <em>The Sisterhood of the Traveling Pants</em> is not a romance, although there are romantic elements of varying degrees in three of the girl's stories. It was refreshing to find the romance taking a backseat to other important issues in a contemporary young adult novel. The four main characters, as well as many of the side characters, were fleshed out and very distinct from one another. I found myself coming to care about all of them. <br /><br />Two things kept this from being a five star read. One was the premise. The idea of magical jeans that fit all four girls perfectly was a bit too silly for me, and I feel that the story could have stood on its own without it. The pants weren't necessary or even integral to the plot. The other reason for the missing star was the writing. I thought it was a bit clunky with adverbs and adjectives galore, and excessive use of dialogue tags when they weren't really needed. It was distracting enough to take me out of the story at times. Otherwise, this was a fantastic read, and I will certainly be reading the sequels. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1683791837889087948">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_973819026">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/973819026" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/11758600-victoria-scott" class="left imgcol" title="Victoria Scott"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1418532331p2/11758600.jpg" alt="Victoria Scott" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/973819026?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 18, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/11758600-victoria-scott" class="user" title="Victoria Scott">Victoria Scott</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/452306.The_Sisterhood_of_the_Traveling_Pants" title="Hardcover 9780385729338" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/11758600-victoria-scott?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/11758600-victoria-scott?shelf=105-challenge-6" class="actionLinkLite">105-challenge-6</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer973819026">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5592269959210033551">This book was on my TBR for way, way too long. In fact, I even watched the movie first! I am so happy I finally got around to reading this<br />I fell in love with their friendship right from the beginning. These four lived for each other, and were completely lost when they were apart. I desperately want a friendship like that. They weren't afraid of anything when they were with each other. Even when they were spread out all over the world, they didn't stop writing, or talking about each other. I abso</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5592269959210033551">This book was on my TBR for way, way too long. In fact, I even watched the movie first! I am so happy I finally got around to reading this<br />I fell in love with their friendship right from the beginning. These four lived for each other, and were completely lost when they were apart. I desperately want a friendship like that. They weren't afraid of anything when they were with each other. Even when they were spread out all over the world, they didn't stop writing, or talking about each other. I absolutely loved that.<br />Individually, some of them were less great. Especially Carmen. Well, okay. Just Carmen.<br />She was SO WHINY. Her dad was newly engaged, to a woman with two kids. So what does Carmen do? Not support her dad. Not make his life any easier. Whine about anything and everything. She did try to talk to him about it. She didn't ask to leave. She just moped around, and ruined a good holiday for everyone. Yeah, he wasn't exactly understanding. He did a few things that deserved a punch in the face. But she could have helped herself. I really, REALLY disliked her.<br />Bee was my favourite. She was so... Vivacious. I've always wanted a chance to use that word, and she is the perfect excuse. Bee is afraid of no one. Rules? Pah. What rules? She fell for her soccer coach, and my God she was going to get him. Nothing was going to stand in her way. She had fantastic hair, so she was going to use it. Her ending broke my heart. She lost a little of her spark because of the mistake she made. And that's not okay! I need my vivacious Bee!<br />Lena was quite sweet. I got annoyed about how much she went on about her prettiness. I know, the point was she fought against that. But she sure did mention it a lot. I loved her little crush on Kostos. I loved how she wouldn't do anything brave about it, for logical reasons. Even though they were totally perfect for each other. I also quite liked her relationship with her grandfather. It wasn't explored much, because he spoke Greek, so conversations were limited. But she really liked him, and looked up to him. Sweet is the only word I can think of to describe her.<br />Tibby's story was probably my favourite, even if she wasn't my favourite character. I lived for the interactions between her and Bailey. Bailey was a little, spunky girl living with cancer. Tibby was so irritated by her to start with. But, of course, Bailey grew on her. How could she not? She irritated me a little in the beginning too, but by the end I just wanted to adopt her. I liked hearing about the suckumentary too. That's a documentary about things that suck, for those of you who don't know. It was cool seeing all the people she met. Especially Brian. Ah, Brian. Tibby was angry at the whole world around her, all the time. But with Bailey around, she wasn't. Fantastic character development!<br />So. We have the whiny one, the vivacious one, the sweet one, the angry one, and a pair of travelling pants. Plus, of course, a bit of romance, some massive character development, and some heartbreaking losses (I'm not saying who!). Do I need to say more?</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5592269959210033551">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer933058237">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1117622426195010118">EDIT: Mayo, 2015<br /><br />No puede creer que tuve que leer este libro para estudiarlo, y analizarlo, y ni siquiera entró en el final que di XD<br /><br /><br />Reseña Original: Diciembre, 2014<br /><br /><br /><strong>3.5</strong><br /><br />Muy entretenido. No pierde tiempo ni párrafos con amores imposibles como eje de la vida de los adolescentes, sino que se toma el trabajo de centrar la historia, no sobre <em>el mundo de una quinceañera girando en torno al resto y como los demás reaccionan a ella</em>, sino más bien sobre como reaccionan las adolescentes a sus propias accion</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1117622426195010118">EDIT: Mayo, 2015<br /><br />No puede creer que tuve que leer este libro para estudiarlo, y analizarlo, y ni siquiera entró en el final que di XD<br /><br /><br />Reseña Original: Diciembre, 2014<br /><br /><br /><strong>3.5</strong><br /><br />Muy entretenido. No pierde tiempo ni párrafos con amores imposibles como eje de la vida de los adolescentes, sino que se toma el trabajo de centrar la historia, no sobre <em>el mundo de una quinceañera girando en torno al resto y como los demás reaccionan a ella</em>, sino más bien sobre como reaccionan las adolescentes a sus propias acciones. Y va más allá incluso: creo que no es solamente una historia sobre una amistad inquebrantable (no que están amigas no tengan esa clase de relación) sino más bien sobre cuatro amigas independizándose la una de la otra, madurando como individuos más allá del refugio que les ofrece ese vínculo que nació cuando ellas mismas nacieron (las madres iban a las mismas clases de parte, por ende, las cuatro se conocen desde que estaban en la panza). Es la historia sobre el primer verano en el que empiezan a moverse solas, sin el sostén de otras personas; el momento en que empiezan a conocerse, realmente, a sí mismas.<br /><br />Lo mejor de la novela son sus protagonistas. Son mujeres de todo tipo, mujeres fuertes, cobardes, imperfectas, ambiciosas, pacíficas, tranquilas, felices, infelices, enamoradizas, no enamoradizas, inteligentes... mujeres de todos los colores... reales. No puedo imaginarme a alguien leyendo esta novela (por más boba que pueda parecerles) sin decir: <em>Mirá, esta es como mengana!!</em> o <em>Conocí a una piba que era así, tal cual</em> o , hasta capaz: <em>Yo hacía lo mismo cuando tenía esa edad</em>... estás en peligro de leer esto y que se te escape un comentario de ese calibre. <br /><br />Creo que está escrito para provocar esa precisa reacción en sus lectores y, por más calculador que pueda ser, la autora pega justo en el blanco.<br /><br />Tenemos cuatro personalidad aparentemente opuestas, ubicadas cada una en cuatro lugares completamente distintos: la "Latina" <strong>Carmen</strong> en una casa suburbana; la <em>cuasi-Amy-March</em>, <strong>Lena</strong>, introvertida y hermosa, de vacaciones en Grecia con abuelos desconocidos; la maníaca (?) <strong>Bridget</strong> en un campamento de soccer, su personalidad <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[probablemente en camino a repetir ciertos aspectos de la personalidad de su madre (supongo que se verá en los libros que sigan) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, Bridget, que no conoce más que blancos y negros, nada de grises; y <strong>Tibby</strong>, la típica <em>rebelde en desarrollo</em>, que se anima a muchas cosas, pero no a la gente que puede llegar a importarle, termina en Wallman lidiando con la clase de gente que más le molesta y lista para filmar su primer <em>documental</em>.<br /><br />Cada lugar funciona casi como un campo de batalla, donde las chicas son puestas para enfrentar, de algún modo, aquello a lo que le temen; es decir, son sacadas de la zona de comfort, para lidiar con lo desconocido; más o menos en una metáfora sobre el crecimiento y la madurez de golpe, frente a lo inesperado: ya sea un amor sorpresivo, una nueva familia, una amistad inesperada y una derrota contra una misma.<br /><br />Si bien es un libro un poco superficial en varios aspectos, y también propenso a resolver conflictos serios a las apuradas (sobre todo llegando al final), es muy divertido y emotivo-- no sólo en las partes obvias <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[<em>Hellooooo , chica de doce años con cancer??</em>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, sino también en escenas donde se trata la relación a punto de romperse entre una hija y un padre; un momento inesperadamente desgarrador con una chica cayendo de golpe de una ilusión gloriosa tras <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[pasar una decepcionante primera vez con un chico más grande <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>... entre otras cosas.<br /><br />Hubo algunas cosas, ciertos aspectos con los que no estoy de acuerdo, que creo deberían haberse tratado con más seriedad o realismo. Sin embargo, ninguno demasiado ofensivo o inaceptable al punto de la ira.<br /><br />El final se resolvió muuuuy a <em>los pedos</em> teniendo en cuenta el tiempo que se usó para armar los conflictos, toda la ira, la tristeza y demás. Creo que la autora tendría que haber agregado al menos veinte páginas más para escribir un desenlace más fuerte y sincero. También me parece que hacía falta más <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[ discusiones entre Carmen y el papá, ya que el que se haya resuelto todo -la envidia, los celos, la irrupción de esta nueva familia suburbana en la vida de los Lowell- casi mágicamente se me hace poco creíble; hacía falta mucho más tiempo para rearmar esa relación. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Sin embargo, el epílogo me pareció lo suficientemente impactante en el sentido de que no lo es. Los últimos párrafos engloban a la perfección la nada misma; el vacío que deja el después de la euforia y la depresión.<br /><br />Las cuatro amigas<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[, juntas de nuevo, pero sin nada que decir. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Muy bueno.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />---------------------------------------<br /><em>[Reseña pendiente]</em><br /><br />Al fin terminado!! Tarde, teniendo en cuenta que el examen es la semana que viene. Tarde, pero seguro. (?)<!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1043351720">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1043351720" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/17243568-karly-the-vampire-ninja-luminescent-monster" class="left imgcol" title="Karly *The Vampire Ninja &amp; Luminescent Monster*"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1451868250p2/17243568.jpg" alt="Karly *The Vampire Ninja &amp; Luminescent Monster*" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1043351720?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 23, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/17243568-karly-the-vampire-ninja-luminescent-monster" class="user" title="Karly *The Vampire Ninja &amp; Luminescent Monster*">Karly *The Vampire Ninja &amp; Luminescent Monster*</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/853137.The_Sisterhood_of_the_Traveling_Pants" title="Paperback 9780440229704" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/17243568-karly-the-vampire-ninja-luminescent-monster?shelf=books-i-loathed" class="actionLinkLite">books-i-loathed</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/17243568-karly-the-vampire-ninja-luminescent-monster?shelf=willow-says-bored-now" class="actionLinkLite">willow-says-bored-now</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1043351720">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9869249939147862222">My review of <em>The Sisterhood of the Traveling Pants</em>.....<br /><br />I understood going into this book that is probably wasn't going to be the book for me. A story of four best friends and the lessons learned on the first summer they spent apart *cue the sappy ass rom-com music* <strong>Whatever!</strong><br /><br />I could sit here and go on and on about all the disasters that happen in this book and why it terrifies me that these "coming of age" stories are so well received by teenage girls but someone has probably done that better tha</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9869249939147862222">My review of <em>The Sisterhood of the Traveling Pants</em>.....<br /><br />I understood going into this book that is probably wasn't going to be the book for me. A story of four best friends and the lessons learned on the first summer they spent apart *cue the sappy ass rom-com music* <strong>Whatever!</strong><br /><br />I could sit here and go on and on about all the disasters that happen in this book and why it terrifies me that these "coming of age" stories are so well received by teenage girls but someone has probably done that better than I. Also, I just don't see how venturing into the headspace of me as a 15 year old is going to be positive for anyone.... so, I'll give a brief synopsis on the four MCs, that I couldn't relate to in any real way, and what I think other girls may see and like in them. <br /><br /><strong>Bridget</strong> is athletic, energetic and goal oriented. She sees something and she just has to attain it, nothing can stand in her way..... even when it's a nineteen year-old coach at her soccer camp. Do.Not.Get.Me.Started.On.How.Stupid.This.Is! Bridget is completely reckless!! Single-minded AND self destructive! <br /><br /><strong>Carmen</strong> is peurto rican - get used to reading this, it is her excuse for all.the.things. - with a hair trigger temper and an absentee father. She feels abandoned and unloved, not surprising feelings, but is so quick to go on the offence that it is impossible to get close enough to care about her. <br /><br /><strong>Lena</strong> is <em>bee-u-T-ful</em>, like a goddess..... she is so beautiful, Oh-my-god .... and hates being seen as merely that. Trust me, I can understand hating being seen as only one aspect of your person but GET.OVER.YOURSELF and show the people another side of you.<br /><br /><img width="500" height="212" class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409850098ra/11029509.gif" /><br /><br />She gives evidence to the theory that shy girls are snobby girls, in a big way. <br /><br /><strong>Tibby</strong> is the lovechild of two parents who eventually grew up and decided they wanted to have a <em>real family</em>. Two siblings under 2 later, and a whole slew of other life changes, have left Tibby missing her previous hippesque lifestyle. <br /><br />I can understand <em>why</em> this could be an interesting story but it just wasn't for me. I found all the MCs voices annoying, not to mention all of their behaviour being self-destructive and crazy. Oh and don't forget insta-love and sappy solutions that make no sense!<br /><br /><img width="320" height="240" class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409847017ra/11029226.gif" /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9869249939147862222">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_143796259">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/143796259" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4877728-melissa" class="left imgcol" title="Melissa"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1388630613p2/4877728.jpg" alt="Melissa" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/143796259?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 26, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4877728-melissa" class="user" title="Melissa">Melissa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/452306.The_Sisterhood_of_the_Traveling_Pants" title="Hardcover 9780385729338" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4877728-melissa?shelf=young-adult" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer143796259">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9944759262349070770">I had seen previews for the movie adaptation of this book and it made me mildly curious. When I found the book on clearance I stopped having excuses on why I hadn't read it yet. I enjoyed the book for the most part, there were a few slow moving areas and a couple things that just made me go "huh?" but otherwise it was definitely a relatable book.<br /><br />Carmen, Bridget (Bee), Tibby, and Lena have been best friends forever. This summer marks the first one that they will be spending time away from each ot</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9944759262349070770">I had seen previews for the movie adaptation of this book and it made me mildly curious. When I found the book on clearance I stopped having excuses on why I hadn't read it yet. I enjoyed the book for the most part, there were a few slow moving areas and a couple things that just made me go "huh?" but otherwise it was definitely a relatable book.<br /><br />Carmen, Bridget (Bee), Tibby, and Lena have been best friends forever. This summer marks the first one that they will be spending time away from each other. Carmen will be visiting her dad, a trip which she is excited to spend one on one time with him. Bridget is going to soccer camp in Mexico. Tibby will have to stay home and work at the local store, something she is entirely not looking forward to. Lastly, Lena will be headed to Greece with her younger sister to stay with their grandparents for the summer. To hold them together, they agree to all ship a special pair of pants to each other throughout the summer, and do great things while wearing them. These pants are so special because, not only are they a thrift store find, they also fit each of the girls perfectly, despite them all being different sizes and body shapes.<br /><br />Lena gets to start and with her, the traveling pants experience a boy wanting to get close to her but then causing problems between her grandparents and their friends. She wants to fix the issues but isn't quite sure how to go about it. Next they travel to Tibby who has befriended a younger girl with Leukemia. The girl drives her nuts but as the summer goes along, she grows closer to this new found friend. Carmen has the next turn and the pants find her lonely and confused at her dad's, where after her plane landed, she discovers that he has a new family; a fiance with two kids just as blond as he is and with whom she doesn't fit in (Carmen is part Puerto Rican). As she grows angrier at being invisible in this beautiful family her temper starts to unleash. Last of all the pants go to Bridget, who has developed a crush on a camp counselor and who has also been just a bit too daring after the death of her mother. After traveling with each of the girls in that order, they also go backwards in the chain and give each girl a chance to rectify her mistakes.<br /><br />The characters were likeable in this book. A girl could identify with any of them at some point and time and the struggles they were experiencing. Tibby was my least favorite. I just didn't connect with her as well as she seemed very immature to me. I probably felt the deepest connect with Carmen and her struggles with her family. What I couldn't understand though was why the author kept having her feel guilty about what she was doing, perhaps it was a little temperamental but in my opinion she had good reason. Her father and his "new family" were horrible from my view. That man should have been very ashamed of himself instead of clueless.<br /><br />The writing of course is geared towards young adults and children so it is very easy to read. There aren't a lot of big words or ideas although there are some tough ones. This book touches on losing virginity, death, and other mature themes and my not be appropriate for very young children. Each chapter starts out with a quote or proverb and while you'd think that each chapter would be centered on girl as they are short chapters; they are not. They skip around from girl to girl and its actually kind of off putting and hard to follow. I think she would have done much better by breaking the girls stories up instead of formatting it the way she did. It caused me to enjoy the book a little less. The story is told in third person for all except the prologue and epilogue, which are narrated by Carmen.<br /><br />It is a good story about growing up and I see it as perfect for younger girls. If I ever chance by the sequel I'll definitely read it.<br /><br />The Sisterhood of the Traveling Pants<br />Copyright 2001<br />294 pages<br /><br />Review by M. Reynard 2011 </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9944759262349070770">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_345297069">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/345297069" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6313653-susan" class="left imgcol" title="Susan"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Susan" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/345297069?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 09, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6313653-susan" class="user" title="Susan">Susan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/452306.The_Sisterhood_of_the_Traveling_Pants" title="Hardcover 9780385729338" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6313653-susan?shelf=2012books" class="actionLinkLite">2012books</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer345297069">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1801765760710173341"><strong>Carmen got the jeans at a thrift shop. They didn’t look all that great: they were worn, dirty, and speckled with bleach. On the night before she and her friends part for the summer, Carmen decides to toss them. But Tibby says they’re great. She'd love to have them. Lena and Bridget also think they’re fabulous. Lena decides that they should all try them on. Whoever they fit best will get them. Nobody knows why, but the pants fit everyone perfectly. Even Carmen (who never thinks she looks good in</strong></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1801765760710173341"><strong>Carmen got the jeans at a thrift shop. They didn’t look all that great: they were worn, dirty, and speckled with bleach. On the night before she and her friends part for the summer, Carmen decides to toss them. But Tibby says they’re great. She'd love to have them. Lena and Bridget also think they’re fabulous. Lena decides that they should all try them on. Whoever they fit best will get them. Nobody knows why, but the pants fit everyone perfectly. Even Carmen (who never thinks she looks good in anything) thinks she looks good in the pants. Over a few bags of cheese puffs, they decide to form a sisterhood and take the vow of the Sisterhood of the Traveling Pants . . . the next morning, they say good-bye. And then the journey of the pants — and the most memorable summer of their lives — begins.</strong><br /><br />I really loved this book. It took a little time to get started and I was beginning to think that it was just another fairly enjoyable teen book - but then it really got going, the characters were fleshed out and I fell in love with all of them. The characterisation was so good! The girls were so different but such complete personalities. Fantastic! I read it in one sitting! I was a bit doubtful about the speed of the postal service (especially to Santorini) but there are times when we just have to suspend belief a little :-)</span>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">10-14 year old girls</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to ClareBear by: </span>
      My sister
