        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer15437484">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer702011666939385771"> READ THE BOOK BEFORE YOU WATCH THE MOVIE. That is, if you watch the movie at all, which I don't reccomend. But the book is romantic and touching. It will make you laugh and cry at the same time. There are four girls who have been friends their whole lives; Bridget (Bee), Carmen, Lena, and Tibby. <br />Bridget is a great soccer player with beautiful blond hair. Carmen is a smart, hot-tempered Puerto Rican who treausures their friendship and works to keep them together. Lena is shy and tries to hide he</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText702011666939385771"> READ THE BOOK BEFORE YOU WATCH THE MOVIE. That is, if you watch the movie at all, which I don't reccomend. But the book is romantic and touching. It will make you laugh and cry at the same time. There are four girls who have been friends their whole lives; Bridget (Bee), Carmen, Lena, and Tibby. <br />Bridget is a great soccer player with beautiful blond hair. Carmen is a smart, hot-tempered Puerto Rican who treausures their friendship and works to keep them together. Lena is shy and tries to hide her external beauty, hoping people will see something other than her pretty features when they look at her. Tibby wants to make a movie, and she is the only one staying at home for the summer. The girls are afraid to each go their seperate ways for the first time in their lives, but a pair of thrift store blue jeans help the girls through everything- together and apart. I reccomend this book to everyone, especially girls 10-14 years old. It is not a fast read, but not a slow one either. It's right inbetween.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16303335139089051455"><blockquote>Nowadays our mothers act like friendship is an elective - falling somewhere down the list after husbands, children, career, home, money. Somewhere between outdoor grilling and music appreciation. That's not how it is for us. My mom tells me, "Just wait till you get serious about boys and school. Just wait till you start competing."   <span style="display:none" id="freeText16303335139089051455"><blockquote>Nowadays our mothers act like friendship is an elective - falling somewhere down the list after husbands, children, career, home, money. Somewhere between outdoor grilling and music appreciation. That's not how it is for us. My mom tells me, "Just wait till you get serious about boys and school. Just wait till you start competing." But she's wrong. We won't let that happen to us.</blockquote><br />This is my sort of YA. It's messy and complicated and funny and smart and honest and <em>real.</em> It's about friendship and family and love. It's about deciding what's important to you and never losing sight of that, no matter how much other things get in the way. It's about life.<br /><br />This is something like my tenth time rereading. And I always read the first three books back to back. This is contemporary YA that proves that real life isn't boring, but joyous and painful and mistake-prone and beautiful and achingly real. </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1147150582">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1147150582" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/24724974-christine" class="left imgcol" title="Christine"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1388062317p2/24724974.jpg" alt="Christine" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1147150582?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 10, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/24724974-christine" class="user" title="Christine">Christine</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/312232.The_Sisterhood_of_the_Traveling_Pants" title="Audio CD 9780739356814" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/24724974-christine?shelf=did-not-finish" class="actionLinkLite">did-not-finish</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/24724974-christine?shelf=audiobook" class="actionLinkLite">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1147150582">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9900956225444830184">The four of them--Carmen, Tibby, Bee and Lena--have been best friends since before they were born, when their moms took a pregnant aerobics class together. Gradually their mothers grew apart, but the four girls grew closer and closer. They have always spent their summer vacations together, creating memories that were intertwined. This year will be different. Carmen is going to stay with her father for the summer. Bee is going to a soccer camp and Lena is going to stay with her grandparents in Gr</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9900956225444830184">The four of them--Carmen, Tibby, Bee and Lena--have been best friends since before they were born, when their moms took a pregnant aerobics class together. Gradually their mothers grew apart, but the four girls grew closer and closer. They have always spent their summer vacations together, creating memories that were intertwined. This year will be different. Carmen is going to stay with her father for the summer. Bee is going to a soccer camp and Lena is going to stay with her grandparents in Greece. Tibby is the only one staying home and working all summer. They are all sad to be separating for the vacation.<br /><br />Then they find an amazing pair of thrift-shop jeans. Despite the radically different body shapes of the four girls, the pants look perfect on every single one of them. These pants must have some sort of magic in them. The girls immediately decide that they will have to use the power of these pants. They draw up a contract stating that the pants shouldn't be washed and they agree to send the pants to each other over the course of the summer, so that each one of them can experience the magic and adventure that is sure to follow such a pair of pants.<br /><br />The book didn't grab me, though. I thought all of the girls were silly and overly dramatic about their lives and the things they had to deal with this summer. The plot lines were predictable, as was the growth and supposed maturity attained by each of the girls during this story.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9900956225444830184">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span id="like_container_review_1147150582" class="likeItContainer"><a href="/rating/voters/1147150582?resource_type=Review" rel="nofollow" id="like_count_review_1147150582"><span class="likesCount">3 likes</span></a> · <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F214438.The_Sisterhood_of_the_Traveling_Pants" class="jsLike like_it gr-button gr-button--small" rel="nofollow">Like</a></span> · <a href="/review/show/1147150582?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1">see review</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_990039521">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/990039521" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/32713007-talina-roma" class="left imgcol" title="Talina  Roma"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1445921550p2/32713007.jpg" alt="Talina  Roma" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/990039521?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 26, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/32713007-talina-roma" class="user" title="Talina  Roma">Talina  Roma</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/452306.The_Sisterhood_of_the_Traveling_Pants" title="Hardcover 9780385729338" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer990039521">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14347147771069040251">Carmen got the jeans at a thrift shop. They didn’t look all that great: they were worn, dirty, and speckled with bleach. On the night before she and her friends part for the summer, Carmen decides to toss them. But Tibby says they’re great. She'd love to have them. Lena and Bridget also think they’re fabulous. Lena decides that they should all try them on. Whoever they fit best will get them. Nobody knows why, but the pants fit everyone perfectly. Even Carmen (who never thinks she looks good in</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14347147771069040251">Carmen got the jeans at a thrift shop. They didn’t look all that great: they were worn, dirty, and speckled with bleach. On the night before she and her friends part for the summer, Carmen decides to toss them. But Tibby says they’re great. She'd love to have them. Lena and Bridget also think they’re fabulous. Lena decides that they should all try them on. Whoever they fit best will get them. Nobody knows why, but the pants fit everyone perfectly. Even Carmen (who never thinks she looks good in anything) thinks she looks good in the pants. Over a few bags of cheese puffs, they decide to form a sisterhood and take the vow of the Sisterhood of the Traveling Pants . . . the next morning, they say good-bye. And then the journey of the pants — and the most memorable summer of their lives — begins.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://s1087.photobucket.com/user/Writer_Girl/media/Writing-1.png.html">
  <img class="escapedImg" alt=" photo Writing-1.png" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414346925i/11642766.png" /></a><br /><br /><br /><br />After starting the first book, I found there was a lot different between the movie and the book. What I love about the movie, did not translate well in the book. I understand the movie will not always be the same as the book, so my review will only be on what I thought about the book itself.<br /><br />I was quite dissapointed with book one. Going in, I had high hopes for this one but I felt let down. I found all of the characters annoying and frustrating, the plot was cliché, and it just didn't intrigue me at all. Keep reading to find out my thoughts on each character.<br /><br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://s1087.photobucket.com/user/Writer_Girl/media/characters-1.png.html">
  <img class="escapedImg" alt=" photo characters-1.png" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414346926i/11642767.png" /></a><br /><br /><br />Carmen: For the summer, Carmen is visiting her Dad who lives up in South Carolina. She rarely gets to see him, so spending the summer with him is extremely exciting for her. What she doesn't expect to see is a blonde lady with two kids waiting at the house for her.<br /><br />I really didn't like Carmen's chapters. She had a terrible temper and it annoyed me sometimes. If I were in her situation, sure, I would be pretty ticked off and hurt. But she over reacted on some occasions and sometimes was uncessarly rude to her step family. All of it just felt..well fake. Her stepfamily trying so hard to be nice, and Carmen trying to do the same but just coming off as a biatch. Carmen was an okay character, but she wasn't my favorite.<br /><br />Tibby: While her three best friend are off to travel the world, Tibby is stuck at home working at Wallmans. She decides to make a suckamentary - a video document of boring people for Tibby to prove how much her summer sucked- On her first day work, she meets this girl Bailey, a twelve year old girl diagnosed with luekemia and it changes her whole summer. <br /><br />I didn't hate Tibby's character, nor did I like her. I felt like she was a whiny teenager that just needed to get over herself. She had the whole 'I hate the world attitude' and it frustated me. If you want to do something for the summer, then get a fun job, do something new, take risks, whatever! But she needed to get over herself. <br /><br />Bridget: For the summer, Bridget is travelling down to Baja California, Mexico for an all girls soccer camp. When she gets there, her eyes are set on one of the teams coaches, Eric. Immediately, she wants him.<br /><br />Bridget was impuslive, reckless and just didn't think things through. When all the girls were getting assigned to their teams, Bridget spots Eric, one of the coaches who is a few years older than her. Bridget can't help but want him, so she does everything in her power to get his attention. Let the wind flow through her hair while she's looking at him, follow him to a bar with a few of friends of hers and dance agaisnt him and other things that just came off as annoying. It made me want to reach inside the book, grab her by the shoulders and yell, "What the fluff is wrong with you? PULL YOURSELF TOGETHER!"<br /><br />She is freaking fifteen years old and he is nineteen. She is a student, and he's the coach. She could care less about him losing his job and her getting kicked out, oh but no, the only thing she cares about is doing the hanky panky with him!<br /><br />I wanted so bad for Bridget to be at the camp for her love for sports. Not for some random dude she just met. This character was a real big disappoint to me.<br /><br />Lena: For the summer, Lena is travelling to Greece to visit her grandparents. Lena is very shy and hates to show off her beauty. Her first few days there her grandmother sets her up with Kostos, a charming friend of the family. He tries his best to get to know her better, but, Lena is wary,and tries to avoid him as much as possible. Problems occur when an iccident happens between Kosto's and Lena, making things difficult between the two familes.<br /><br /><br />I found Lena to be very dull. All she did was paint, sketch, or walk around the house and city. She just didn't draw me in. I was hoping the book would be like the movie. I hoped that she would talk to him, go on small adventures with him, and actually fall in love with him the right way. Not ignore him the whole summer, and then tell you love him when you're about to leave. I found that to be so idiotic. How can you fall in love with someone you don't even know?! Like all the other characters, I just wasn't interested.<br /><br />I'm thankful the movie came out better than the first book. I'm currently reading the second book, and so far it's okay.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_902540686">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/902540686" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/21507553-sofia" class="left imgcol" title="Sofia "><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1439169859p2/21507553.jpg" alt="Sofia " /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/902540686?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 11, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/21507553-sofia" class="user" title="Sofia ">Sofia </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/21507553-sofia?shelf=contemporary" class="actionLinkLite">contemporary</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21507553-sofia?shelf=2014-reads" class="actionLinkLite">2014-reads</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21507553-sofia?shelf=young-adult" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21507553-sofia?shelf=book-club" class="actionLinkLite">book-club</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer902540686">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15622637053998115689"><strong> Disclaimer: I did not read the whole book. I read about 75% of it and then just skipped to the end. My thoughts on this book are a reflection of the portions I did read (which was most of it, trolls, so back off.) </strong><br />Hmmm. Well, this was a curious little book indeed. I'm not sure if I was surprised or disappointed; I was a mix of both. My feelings for this book can be summed up in one word: <em> meh. </em> <br />The Sisterhood of the Traveling Pants was a book for book club. As soon as I heard the name "Sisterho</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15622637053998115689"><strong> Disclaimer: I did not read the whole book. I read about 75% of it and then just skipped to the end. My thoughts on this book are a reflection of the portions I did read (which was most of it, trolls, so back off.) </strong><br />Hmmm. Well, this was a curious little book indeed. I'm not sure if I was surprised or disappointed; I was a mix of both. My feelings for this book can be summed up in one word: <em> meh. </em> <br />The Sisterhood of the Traveling Pants was a book for book club. As soon as I heard the name "Sisterhood of the Traveling Pants", I was like: <br /><br /><img width="300" height="300" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397916399i/9345902._SX540_.png" /><br /><br />Yeah. I mean, c'mon. Does that title look particularly grabbing? <br />The synopsis was even worse. Four girls, tied by EFFING PANTS THAT ALL FIT THEM? Whoa, magic. <br /><br /><img width="200" height="200" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385244491i/7105773._SX540_.gif" /><br /><em> Morgan Freeman knows my thoughts exactly! Now that's magic...</em><br /><br />Moving on then...<br />So the book focuses on four girls: Lena, Tibby, Bridget, and Carmen, and their first summer apart. However, they are able to sort of...connect?...because of a pair of pants that fits them all (even though Tibby is super small, Bridget is tall and slim, Carmen is curvy, and Lena is...whatever). They decide that even though they will be in different places (Lena in Greece, Carmen in South Carolina, Bridget in Mexico, and Tibby at home), they will send the pants to each other and it will be a way of feeling their presence, if you will. <br /><br /><strong> Lena </strong><br /><br />What I liked about Lena's chapters was that <em> Lena was aware that she was beautiful. </em> Her friends constantly referred to her as the beauty, and Lena was confident that she was pretty. I liked that a lot.<br />But Lena herself was a bland character. Okay, so she likes to paint. And is wary of love and boys and all that. Cool. And...? <br />I just didn't get a good enough feel for Lena's character, and I wasn't emotionally connected to her. I didn't <em> care </em> if she and Kostos hit it off. I didn't <em> care </em> about her awkwardness with her bapi (grandfather.) I just didn't care.<br />I also didn't particularly look forward to Lena's chapters because they were boy-centric. They focused on the romance between Lena and a Greek boy named Kostos (who is a pretty lovely young man, I must admit.) I, simply, am not interested in those story lines.<br />The setting of Greece was portrayed well; I could feel the atmosphere and all of the places Lena went to. I just wished I could've seen more. <br /><br /><strong> Carmen </strong><br /><br />I liked her chapters, and I liked Carmen. Carmen snaps. She loses her temper. She hates people who don't deserve her hate. She is just so flawed, and I <em> freaking loved her. </em> <br />Carmen's story: she is visiting her dad, Al, who is divorced. She can't wait to spend a summer with him since she doesn't get to see him, but soon learns that Al has a new blonde (Carmen is Puerto Rican), perfect family: he's getting married.<br />Carmen's alienation, her feeling of being invisible, her resentment towards her new family and her refusal to be mad at her dad is handled so realistically and so well. Carmen's story was my favorite, IMO. The way she interacted with her stepfamily, her stepfamily trying so hard to be nice to Carmen, to be cordial to Carmen. I really liked Carmen and her chapters.<br /><br /><strong> Tibby </strong><br /><br />Tibby's staying at home, working at Wallman's. As she says, she's dying a "slow death at Wallman's." She decides that during her summer, she's going to make a suckamentary (a documentary of a bunch of weird and/or boring people that chronicles how much Tibby's summer sucked.) But her whole summer changes when she meets Bailey, a twelve-year-old girl diagnosed with leukemia.<br />What I really liked is that Bailey is not typically likable when Tibby first meets her. In fact, Tibby shouts at Bailey when Bailey accuses her of stealing money from her wallet. And when Tibby first hangs out with Bailey, she only does so because: <br /><br /><em> "Are you just being nice to me because I have cancer?" she asked over her shoulder.<br />Tibby considered this for a moment. She could lie some more. Or not. She shrugged. "Yeah, I guess so." </em><br /><br />I liked Tibby also, though not nearly as much as I loved Carmen. She's a pretty strong character, and you get a grasp on her personality: she's direct, ruthless, rebellious, but much more than that. <br /><br /><strong> Bridget </strong><br /><br />I saved Bridget's for last because I have a lot to say about this one. Let me just say it straight: <strong>I. DID. NOT. LIKE. BRIDGET. </strong> I didn't. I hated reading her chapters. Bridget is in Baja California, Mexico, at an all-girls' soccer camp. When she gets there, she immediately falls in love with a coach...Eric. And so <em> all </em> of Bridget's chapters are pretty much devoted to Bridget pursuing Eric. <br />Does that seem like something that would interest me?<br /><br /><img width="300" height="300" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1381525445i/4981089._SY540_.jpg" /><br /><br />Bridget is reckless. She's impulsive. She doesn't <em> think. </em> She is literally falling in head-over-heels insta-love with a coach, whom she's not allowed to start a romantic relationship with. Ooh, star-crossed love! *rolls eyes* <br />She keeps trying to have sex with Eric, even though HE'S A COACH AND SHE'S FIFTEEN. Not only does she disregard the rules, she keeps putting Eric in danger of losing his job. If she really loved him, she would not keep pursuing him. Now, I love when characters make mistakes and when they learn from them (which Bridget ultimately did), but I did not like following Bridget.<br />Here's the thing about Bridget: we are <em> told </em> that Bridget is athletic and loves soccer. Yet when Bridget does well at camp, it's all motivated by <em> Eric. </em> Eric is her driving force. What about her ambition? Her love for sports? <br />The thing that disappointed me was that Bridget's story had a lot of potential. Her mother died (and it is hinted that it is because of suicide, depression, mental illness, you get the picture.) Yet NONE of that is explored. The whole story is devoted to Bridget and Eric.<br /><br /><strong> Other things: </strong><br /><br />The writing? Okay. There was one instance where Brashares described Baja as having "protective mountains." Try drawing that. I dare you. <br />Also, just something you should know: the book starts with a first-person prologue from Carmen and ends with a first-person epilogue from Carmen. In between, it shifts between the four characters...in third-person. It's a bit jarring at first.<br />There was one quote (I can't find it) where Carmen pretty much labels all her friends (Bridget the athlete, Tibby the rebel, Lena the beauty) and comments that she can't seem to categorize herself. I wanted to scream, "YOU CANNOT CATEGORIZE YOURSELF, YOU CANNOT CATEGORIZE ANYONE!" People do not just live in neat little labels. <br />I didn't hate Sisterhood; I didn't. But I can't give it more than a two stars because it was just meh. Perhaps it could've gotten a three stars had Bridget's chapters not annoyed me so much. It was more substantial than I expected, yet I felt had so much more potential than it explored. <br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/35988179" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1647757-colleen" class="left imgcol" title="Colleen"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Colleen" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/35988179?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 21, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1647757-colleen" class="user" title="Colleen">Colleen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/452306.The_Sisterhood_of_the_Traveling_Pants" title="Hardcover 9780385729338" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">no one</span></div>

        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer35988179'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer35988179">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8135765468993194821">I read the Sisterhood of the Traveling Pants today, and I'm kind of sorry. It might have been interesting when I was a teenager, but the now-me found it rather choppy and trivial. The coming-of-age theme is great, as is the idea of The Pants having their own kind of magic. But the issues of love, family, death were so chopped up and interspersed that I had trouble investing myself in any of the characters. <br /><br />I admit that the theme of truthfulness-to-self was as interesting as it was irritating. Th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8135765468993194821">I read the Sisterhood of the Traveling Pants today, and I'm kind of sorry. It might have been interesting when I was a teenager, but the now-me found it rather choppy and trivial. The coming-of-age theme is great, as is the idea of The Pants having their own kind of magic. But the issues of love, family, death were so chopped up and interspersed that I had trouble investing myself in any of the characters. <br /><br />I admit that the theme of truthfulness-to-self was as interesting as it was irritating. The so-perfect-but-not Lena and Bridget compared badly to the trying-to-cope-but-can't Tibby and Carmen. As soon as Bailey was introduced, I started comparing the story (unfavorably) with A Time for Dancing. I thought ATfD was a painfully real story, with sympathetic characters and an easy style to read. The Sisterhood was painfully real in some of the scenes, but unreal in how the characters (except Bridget) had to face An Event and reconcile to it. Nope, sorry, I can't see Lydia allowing her picture-perfect wedding with her picture-perfect family get interrupted by ... well, basically, forgiveness doesn't look real when the characters doing it are barely penciled in and have no depth from which to bring it.<br /><br />I can rest content with the knowledge that I now have absolutely no interest in seeing the movie or reading the sequel. Yes, comments are open. Let the beating begin.</span>

Abia a?tept s? v?d filmele ?i s? citesc celelalte volume. <br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1214471005">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13886939939923582931">The Sisterhood of the Traveling Pants follows a group of friends Carmen, Lena, Tibby and Bridget as they spend their summers apart. The day before they part ways, they find a pair of pants that fit them all perfectly. What is this madness, you say? Thus begins the journey of the Pants from D.C to Santorini Greece, Charleston, Baja California and back. The girls experience an unforgettable summer and only the Pants know everything.<br /><br />TSotTP was a delightful read! I especially loved Tibby's journey a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13886939939923582931">The Sisterhood of the Traveling Pants follows a group of friends Carmen, Lena, Tibby and Bridget as they spend their summers apart. The day before they part ways, they find a pair of pants that fit them all perfectly. What is this madness, you say? Thus begins the journey of the Pants from D.C to Santorini Greece, Charleston, Baja California and back. The girls experience an unforgettable summer and only the Pants know everything.<br /><br />TSotTP was a delightful read! I especially loved Tibby's journey and she was the one that stayed at their hometown! Her story was inspiring and made me teary but in a good way. I loved how the Pants gave each individual strength and courage when the other girls could not physically be there for them. The Pants really are magical!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14731502697256188274">my youngest sister got this for me for christmas. i admit it took me a while to pick it up, mostly because the premise seemed so ridiculous. <br /><br />but then i read it. and i fell in love: with carmen's temper, and lena's hidden feelings, and EFFIE, and BEE's misdirected passion, and tibby's cynical nature crossed with bailey's infinite wisdom and brian at the dragon master video machine. <br /><br />i love the septembers. i adore their friendship, and their letters, and the way they are there for each other, and t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14731502697256188274">my youngest sister got this for me for christmas. i admit it took me a while to pick it up, mostly because the premise seemed so ridiculous. <br /><br />but then i read it. and i fell in love: with carmen's temper, and lena's hidden feelings, and EFFIE, and BEE's misdirected passion, and tibby's cynical nature crossed with bailey's infinite wisdom and brian at the dragon master video machine. <br /><br />i love the septembers. i adore their friendship, and their letters, and the way they are there for each other, and the cheesy rituals. something about me understands them, so intensely - maybe because i have three sisters myself? but. i love this book, and i love these girls. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BkvKDTon0Lpof/xaBX+7KEIgta2zr/9/Kq7Ljf3j2zVjn/XeyPXEQOSniOF7Hl2aC9d2tPpyuNVAp84fMXYtcA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KZn1MpVNTDqpMfjfBOo7u7c5JMOduB4ve+TnMJ9L1JpMTcrhZ59YwCXpjGR6i90J/s7n2tRlWYUR7eKiU94i3w==')})

Readers learn quickly that each girl has her own writing style and that at two of the Brookfield boys (Seb and Charlie) seem to be smitten with Lydia and Emily. The only trouble is Cassie\'s pen pal, Matthew, a shady character who first sends her short, threatening letters and then becomes strangely sweet toward her. Nobody can figure out why Cassie keeps writing to him, but after she has a crushing meet-up with Matthew, Cassie discovers -- with the help of her friends and the Brookfield guys -- that he hasn\'t been honest about his identity. All could be ended there, but when Charlie helps take revenge and Brookfield High gets mysteriously vandalized, the group comes together to deliver justice and save the endangered pen pal project.\n\nFresh and impressive, Moriarty\'s novel is lighthearted fare that will keep readers glued to the end. In particular, her knack for capturing different writing styles shines the spotlight on her own talent, giving audiences clear inspiration to try their own diary or journal writing. Clearly centered on the girls while incorporating romance and fun guy personalities -- Rachel Cohn and Meg Cabot fans will eat this up. Now fans of Angus, Thongs and Full-Frontal Snogging -- Georgia\'s first set of hilarious musings on life -- can get another peek into the mind of this wryly inquisitive English lass in the appealing sequel: On the Bright Side, I\'m Now the Girlfriend of a Sex God.\n\nAs the title implies, Georgia has snagged herself a sex god in the form of Robbie, the boy of her dreams. Now that they\'ve indulged in a bit of &amp;quot;full-frontal snogging,&amp;quot; Georgia turns her attention to advancing the relationship. But things quickly go wrong when she learns that her father\'s new job may necessitate a move to New Zealand. Crestfallen, Georgia feels her life might as well be over. Then, miraculously, the dreaded move is cancelled, and things seem to be getting better -- at least until 17-year-old Robbie decides to break up with Georgia because he\'s bothered by the difference in their ages. \n\nBorrowing freely from her mum\'s closet and advice books, even as she\'s steadfastly discounting everything her mum says, a crushed but determined Georgia comes up with a scheme to win Robbie back. As usual, nothing goes as planned, and life is further complicated by Georgia\'s temperamental cat, Angus (who\'s having a few amorous leanings of his own), and her baby sister, Libby, whose fascination with (and lack of control over) her bodily functions leads to several intriguing mishaps. Of course, there are other disasters, too: a quick-tan lotion that turns Georgia\'s legs orange, a run-in with the aptly named Bummer sisters, and friends who insist on focusing on their own problems from time to time.\n\nWho knew the angst of adolescence could be so much fun? This Georgia\'s-eye view of teenage life is wonderfully egocentric and side-splittingly funny. And despite the occasional language barrier (a glossary of terms is provided in the back of the book), Georgia\'s thoughts and experiences will prove universally recognizable to anyone who is, or has     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3681.Ann_Brashares">About Ann Brashares</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/3681.Ann_Brashares"><img alt="3681" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1208391697p2/3681.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer3525030201510350217">Ann Brashares grew up in Chevy Chase, Maryland, with three brothers and attended a Quaker school in the D.C. area called Sidwell Friends. She studied Philosophy at Barnard College, part of Columbia University in New York City. Expecting to continue studying philosophy in graduate school, Ann took a year off after college to work as an editor, hoping to save money for school. Loving her job, she ne</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3525030201510350217">Ann Brashares grew up in Chevy Chase, Maryland, with three brothers and attended a Quaker school in the D.C. area called Sidwell Friends. She studied Philosophy at Barnard College, part of Columbia University in New York City. Expecting to continue studying philosophy in graduate school, Ann took a year off after college to work as an editor, hoping to save money for school. Loving her job, she never went to graduate school, and instead, remained in New York City and worked as an editor for many years. Ann made the transition from editor to full-time writer with her first novel, <a title=" The Sisterhood of the Traveling Pants" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20The%20Sisterhood%20of%20the%20Traveling%20Pants"> The Sisterhood of the Traveling Pants</a>. Ann and her husband live with their three children in New York.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3525030201510350217">...more</a>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/3681.Ann_Brashares" class="actionLink moreLink">More about Ann Brashares...</a>
